Local News

Yesterday's Rampant Autumn Sun 116

Afternoon Temperature Reaches 104 Degrees

Two New Records for the Observatory

Hospital Clinics are Busy Again

According to the National News Agency, the climate in Shanghai this year has been marked by drought and heat. On July 12th, the extreme heat reached 104.4 degrees, setting a new record for the observatory in its 63 years. It was hoped that the weather would cool down after the start of autumn. Unexpectedly, after the highest temperature reached 100 degrees the day before yesterday, it exceeded that again yesterday, suddenly increasing to 104 degrees, only 0.4 degrees lower than the hottest day last month. Yesterday afternoon, between noon and 2:30 PM, those sitting in offices were all sweating profusely. Looking up at the sky, it was a clear blue with not a single cloud. Sunlight radiated intensely on the roads, and the rickshaw pullers and laborers were panting, their clothes soaked with sweat. According to the observatory, the highest recorded temperature in August in its 63 years was 102.9 degrees, so this year has already set two new records.

Due to the recent hot weather, the clinics at various epidemic hospitals have been busier. For example, the Shanghai Epidemic Hospital on Xizang Road is still seeing nearly 200 outpatients every day. The most common symptoms are vomiting and diarrhea, followed by dysentery and malaria. Cases of heatstroke have become rare. There were still four deaths the day before yesterday, but none yesterday. In addition, the Emergency Epidemic Hospital on Kaifeng Road sees about 60 to 70 outpatients daily, with dysentery and gastroenteritis (i.e., vomiting and diarrhea) being the most common. There were two cases of heatstroke yesterday. The number of deaths has decreased. The Hongkou Epidemic Hospital still sees 300 outpatients daily, mostly with dysentery.

Regarding the drought inland, according to experienced farmers, such a drought in the Jiangnan region only occurred once before, in the sixth year of the Xianfeng era, but it was not as extremely hot. They also say that in recent days, thick fog has often filled the air in the evening. According to farmers' proverbs, spring fog means rain, summer fog means heat, autumn fog means a cool breeze, and winter fog means snow. Now, there is fog in autumn, but it is extremely hot, which is said to be autumn behaving like summer, an abnormal climate. It is truly a rare climate phenomenon that has not been seen in decades.

The Severe Drought Urgently Needs Food 117

Foreign Rice Orders Not Yet Complete

Flour Prices Skyrocket

According to the Daily News, due to the prolonged drought and lack of rain, rice prices have been soaring. Banks and rice merchants in Shanghai have ordered more than one million dan of foreign rice. Provinces affected by the drought are also purchasing large quantities from Shanghai. Flour prices have been rising sharply in recent days, which is also related to the drought.

Continuing to Order Foreign Rice According to rice industry sources yesterday, the current orders for foreign rice, placed by banks and rice merchants, are motivated by the desire to regulate the food supply for the people. The amount, reported to be over one million dan, is indeed accurate. Recently, there have been many provinces coming to Shanghai to purchase rice, and local sales are also brisk. Prices are being set as low as possible, so current sales are only covering costs. However, the exploitation of profiteering merchants is inevitable. The Social Affairs Bureau is conducting strict investigations and registrations to prevent this. Currently, the orders placed with foreign merchants for foreign rice in the past three days total about 100,000 dan. The rice is mostly of lower quality, and the prices are about the same as before. It is expected to arrive in Shanghai at the beginning of next month.

Difficulty in Stabilizing Rice Prices The import of foreign rice and the domestic rice trade have not had a significant impact on the current situation. Most of the foreign rice is being sold inland, where it is truly needed. Currently, only a dozen or so rice boats from inland areas are arriving in Shanghai daily. Rice merchants' inventories are dwindling, with only a portion remaining unsold. The demand for rice is even greater after autumn as the drought intensifies, so it is quite difficult to stabilize rice prices.

Flour Prices Rise and Sales are Brisk In April of this year, the price of flour was only 1.25 yuan per bag, which was below cost. At that time, manufacturers reported significant losses and requested government assistance. Since the start of the drought, market prices have risen continuously. Recently, they have skyrocketed from 1.90 yuan to 2.70 yuan per bag. Due to large-scale purchases by banks, prices have continued to soar. Daily transactions have remained above one million bags. Flour mills have also significantly increased their output.

Fellow Countrymen from Haining in Shanghai 118

Yesterday's Disaster Relief Meeting

A Resolution to Request One Million Yuan in Public Bonds from the Provincial Government for Relief

In addition to Fundraising, Warehouses Will be Allocated for Loans First

Zhejiang Province is suffering from a severe drought this year, especially Haining County. Fellow countrymen from Haining in Shanghai held a meeting at the Silk Cocoon Guild yesterday afternoon at 3 PM to discuss disaster relief. They resolved to request one million yuan in relief from the provincial government. Details are as follows:

Attendees The following Haining natives attended the meeting: Jiang Huiyue, Wang Peisan, Shen Mianfu, Huang Yiqin, Wu Wanli, Wang Jinsheng, Xu Xingbin, Xu Shenru, Zheng Peiheng, Gu Dayi, Zhan Yongquan, Ju Yihong, Wang Weigeng, Yan E'sheng, Yu Kuangluo, Xu Shaojiu, Shi Shaochu, Wang Xufu, Wang Luhua, Hua Liting, Chen Gengyu, Zha Zhongjian, Zhang Zhengxue, Xu Yongzuo, Shen Huachen, and more than sixty others.

Chairman's Report Chairman Xu Shenru reported that after the disaster relief fundraising in the 21st year of the Republic, there was a surplus of 28,500 yuan, which was handed over to the Renshen Relief Surplus Management Committee. By this year, with interest, the total amount is just under 30,000 yuan. This year, Gengning County has had no rain during the plum rain season, and there has been a severe drought in summer and autumn, leading to withered crops and no secondary products. There is no hope for the autumn harvest, and the people's livelihood is in dire straits. There is no one to turn to for help. Shenru and others recently went to Beijing to petition, and the authorities agreed to provide relief, but the disaster is extremely severe, and help is urgently needed. It is now planned to first organize an emergency relief association to raise funds for industrial relief and shelters, and the previous relief surplus can also be used within the original scope to ensure that it is used appropriately.

Representatives' Speeches Next, County Magistrate Jiang Huiyue of the county said that since the beginning of summer this year, there has not been a drop of rain, causing the land in Ning to crack and the rivers to dry up. The autumn harvest is hopeless, and the plight of the residents is unspeakable. I believe everyone is aware of this. Under such extreme hardship, there have been incidents of robbery of rice and grain in Changan, Xiashi, and Yuanhua. For the sake of security, the government has had to impose severe punishments. Although things are calmer now, there are still hungry people waiting to be fed. If concrete relief measures are not taken first, the 360,000 people of Ning County will face certain death. However, relief is a major undertaking, and it cannot be effective without collective efforts. I hope everyone will do their duty and gather large sums of money to save the people of the entire county, etc.

Resolutions The following resolutions were then discussed and passed: (1) Officially appoint representatives to petition the Zhejiang Provincial Government to allocate one million yuan in public bonds for relief. (2) County warehouses and district warehouses should all first provide loans. A letter should be sent by the county government to the Department of Civil Affairs, starting with investigating the poorest households. (3) District grain reserves should be instructed to be lent out locally, and a letter should be sent to the county government to order each district to do so. (4) Several nursing homes should be established for widows, widowers, orphans, and the disabled, and they should be accommodated as much as possible. The funds should be allocated from the Renshen relief surplus. (5) The method for further fundraising in various places will be discussed after the amounts have been obtained.

Nomination of Committee Members The following committee members were then nominated: Shen Mianfu, Shi Shaochu, Zhang Xinfu, Li Yingbo, Shen Jinru, Wu Xinmu, Shen Shuying, Li Hongxiang, Wu Yugeng, Zhu Zemin, Huang Yiqin, Zha Zhongqian, Feng Liutang, Wang Jinsheng, Xu Tiru, Zhu Linzun, Wang Peisan, Yang Xuemen, Gu Dayi, Yu Kuangluo, Zhu Rongtang, Xu Xingbin, Tang Yongfu, Xu Shaozeng, Zhu Jun, Zhang Binren, Zhang Lengseng, Shen Zhongyue, Zhou Yuemin, Xu Shenru, Shen Huachen, Xu Yushu, Pan Gengsheng, Yao Wenfu, Xu Lingyun, Chen Yugeng, Chen Songlin, Zhou Wusan, Xu Boming, Wang Luping, Gu E'sheng, Chen Gengyu, Ye Shantao, Yang Jixin, Zhu Yanqing, Yu Wuyun, Zhang Xinchu, Gu Yigu, Zhang Xinqi, Zhu Xiaoqin, Yu Zhiqing, Hua Liting, Wang Xufu, Zhang Youyi, Ju Yihong, Wang Weigeng, and Hang Zhuoying.

Executive Staff Fifteen executive committee members were then mutually elected: Jiang Huiyue, Zhan Yongquan, Xu Shenru, Xu Xingbin, Zhang Binren, Shen Zhongyue, Shen Huachen, Xu Yushu, Zha Zhongjian, Zhou Wusan, Gu Dayi, Shi Shaochu, Yan E'sheng, Pan Gengsheng, and Wang Luping. The following staff members were also nominated: (1) General Affairs: Gu Dayi, Hang Zhuoying, Wu Yugeng; (2) Finance: Zhou Wusan, Ju Yihong, Wang Weigeng; (3) Supervision: Zhan Yongquan, Xu Yushu, Zha Zhongjian.

Report on Disaster Conditions Yesterday, County Magistrate Jiang Huiyue told a reporter from the New Sound News Agency that our county is unfortunate and has suffered repeated disasters. The silk industry has been in decline for a long time, and the coffers have long been empty. In the 21st year of the Republic, the rural economy collapsed, and the disaster became severe. There was a period of food scarcity, leading to rice looting incidents. Fellow countrymen raised funds for relief, which helped the people adjust, and the unrest subsided. This year, there has been a prolonged drought during the plum rain season, and even the grass has withered. In terms of the people's food, the crops have withered, and there is no hope for the autumn harvest. In terms of secondary products, the silk industry has declined, and both cotton and beans have failed. People's livelihoods are in dire straits, and there is no one to turn to for help. He was moved to tears when describing the disaster. Haining County has a total area of 800,000 mu and a population of 360,000. The disaster has created a scene of scorched earth. The city rivers are completely dry, and drinking water is almost exhausted. People mainly eat soybeans and wheat, and some struggle to find enough to eat all day long, leading to numerous suicides. Rice prices have soared, increasing by three yuan compared to before. The water in the Qiantang River has excessive salinity, making it useless for drinking or irrigation. The most critical issue at the moment is fire prevention. If a fire were to break out, there would be no way to extinguish it. He hopes that the central government can implement relief measures as soon as possible to restore the people's livelihoods, etc.

Fundraising Announcement The association also passed a fundraising announcement, which states, "Poetry echoes the chapter of the Cloud Han, 'How severe is the drought?' The people look to the rivers and lakes for moisture, hoping to avoid hunger. Our Haining, formerly Yanguan, is located in saline-alkali land. It has no large bodies of water for storage and relies solely on sluice gates to distribute small streams. It is always affected by droughts and floods. Rice is not enough for self-sufficiency, and people rely on buying rice for meals. Silk is a major secondary product, and trade in silk is essential for livelihood. Unexpectedly, sales have been sluggish for a long time, and many factories have been closed. Over the past three or four years, the few tens of millions in income have been used to address accumulated difficulties. Now, we are suffering from a severe drought. The plum rain season has been prolonged, and even the grass has withered. Incidents of rice looting are frequent, and there is no hope for relief. People are suffering from hunger and cold, and there is no one to turn to for help. Alas, pictures depict displaced people, and we cannot bear to see starving corpses in the fields. There are many virtuous people in the world who will surely donate grain from their granaries. Blessings are not in vain. Wealth is dispersed, and the people will gather. Goodness brings abundance, and sincerity will surely be rewarded. We hope that influential figures across the country and kind people from our hometown will open their hearts and wallets and contribute to the cause. Merit is like building a pagoda, and the fame and fragrance will spread throughout the humble dwellings. Respectfully announced."

Jiangsu Province Shanghai City 119

Decision to Dredge Songjiang River

Jiangsu Province Collects Labor Tax, Allocates 80,000 Yuan Annually

Shanghai City Handles it Separately Through the Dredging Bureau and the Municipal Government

Regarding the method of dredging the Wusong River, the Taihu Basin Water Conservancy Committee had previously drafted a construction plan and budget, and requested the National Economic Commission to allocate funds under the cotton and wheat loan. Half a year has passed, and the allocation has not yet been approved. However, the Wusong River urgently needs dredging and cannot be delayed any longer. It is now heard that the dredging method has been separately agreed upon by the Ministry of Interior, the Jiangsu Provincial Government, and the Shanghai Municipal Government. The details are as follows:

Provincial and Municipal Division of Dredging According to the New Sound News Agency in Beijing, it has now been decided that the dredging of the Wusong River will be undertaken separately by the Jiangsu Provincial Government and the Shanghai Municipal Government. The section within the jurisdiction of Jiangsu Province, from Guajingkou in the upper reaches of the Wusong River to Laopanlonggang, which is the upper reaches of the river, will be the responsibility of the Jiangsu Provincial Government. The labor tax collection method will be adopted, similar to the Liutang River project, and it will be completed in three phases. The funds required cannot be obtained by clearing the previous Wusong River dredging mu tax, so 80,000 yuan will have to be allocated annually from the road construction surtax in eight counties to cover it. The section within the Shanghai city area, from Laopanlonggang in the lower reaches to the outlet, which is the lower reaches of the river, will be handled separately by the Municipal Government, except for the two sites of Yujidun and Fanwangdu, where the straightening of bends will be arranged by the Municipal Government. The rest will be continued to be contracted by the Dredging Bureau through the Municipal Government.

Municipal Government Measures It is also reported from Shanghai that the Municipal Government estimates that the labor costs required for the straightening of bends at the two sites of Yujidun and Fanwangdu will be approximately 200,000 yuan. In addition to the 50,000 yuan allocated by the Municipal Government, the remaining 150,000 yuan will be raised by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce in conjunction with the Shipping Association and the Inland River Steamboat Industry Association. The Municipal Government Secretariat has issued a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to handle this matter.

Chamber of Commerce's Response The Municipal Chamber of Commerce has stated that the Wusong River within the city area, from Xinzha Bridge to the Outer Baidu Bridge outlet, was dredged by the former Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, which was responsible for fundraising, as early as the 13th year of the Republic. However, due to a shortage of funds and the large scale of the project, it was difficult to complete. The mu tax from various counties has not been allocated as scheduled, and the outstanding amount has been borrowed by the Chamber of Commerce. As of now, the principal and interest owed amount to more than 170,000 yuan, which has not been repaid and is a heavy burden. If the aforementioned outstanding amount can be allocated in full, the Chamber of Commerce can consider donating some funds to help with the project. However, in these times of economic downturn, it is truly difficult to raise funds from various industries.

Resolution of the Sailor Issue

No Dutch Sailors Hired

Decision to Use Domestic Sailors

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company borrowed from the British Boxer Indemnity Fund to build four seagoing vessels in the UK. With the start of operations approaching, the issue of hiring sailors, including Dutch sailors and domestic sailors, has arisen. Dutch Envoy's Recommendation The Dutch shipowner, Boerger & Flower, stopped operation due to poor business, the Dutch ambassador stationed in China had recommended to China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to sell their ship to them, but was denied. Overseas Chinese in Singapore 125

Lin Cangsong is Expelled

Heartbreak Over the National Crisis Leads to the Authorities' Anger

Detained for Three Months and then Repatriated

According to the National News Agency, overseas Chinese are increasingly subjected to harsh oppression by local governments and natives. They dare to be angry but dare not speak out. The status of overseas Chinese is no longer what it used to be. This is due to the weakness of the country and the lack of effective solutions from the authorities, so they are often left to fate. Yesterday, Mr. Lin Cangsong, an overseas Chinese residing in Singapore, was even detained for three months and then repatriated for his heartbreak over the national crisis, which aroused the anger of the authorities. When the reporter met Mr. Lin at his residence yesterday and asked about the expulsion, he couldn't help but sob repeatedly. According to Mr. Lin, he was an overseas student in Singapore, British Malaya, and graduated from the local Chinese High School. However, due to his poor family circumstances, he had to drop out of school and take a job at the Dao Nan Primary School, which was run by Fujianese in Singapore. After the September 18th Incident in Shenyang, the rich three northeastern provinces were forcibly occupied by the violent Japanese. He was extremely indignant. Thinking that every citizen is responsible for the rise and fall of the country, he could not rush to the battlefield, but he should still fulfill his national obligations. Therefore, he often wrote articles in newspapers to awaken his fellow overseas Chinese and jointly save the situation. Unexpectedly, this aroused the anger of the local government, which labeled him a radical and arrested him, detaining him for three months and then deporting him. He suffered this humiliation and felt grief and anger. He had no choice but to return to China quietly. Moreover, before he was expelled, all his clothes were searched and taken away. After arriving in Shanghai, he had almost nothing to support himself. Fortunately, the socialite Mr. Huang Jingwan generously donated money to send him back to his hometown. This kindness and virtue are indeed touching. However, he is determined to have a day to serve his country and hopes that his compatriots in the motherland will work hard to prevent the extinction of the Chinese race.

Familiar Financier 128

Qiu Jicai Discusses Silver Price Fluctuations

Our Country's Silver is Bound to Continue Flowing Out

The Relationship Between Silver Price Fluctuations and the Great War

According to the Central News Agency, since the US government raised the price of silver and nationalized silver holdings, our country's silver exports have reached over 100 million yuan. This matter is of great importance to the national economy and social finance. The Ministry of Finance has now hired experts to study countermeasures. A Central News Agency reporter inquired with Mr. Qiu Jicai, who is familiar with financial matters, and he said the following:

Large-Scale Silver Outflow from Our Country: The fluctuation of silver prices in London differs little from the market price in Shanghai. Normally, the difference is only one-sixteenth of a penny. This time, due to the US government buying silver and raising its price, the difference between the two places has reached a significant two pence. As a result, our country's large-scale silver exports have reached 100 million. It is predicted that a large amount of silver will continue to flow out, because the difference in silver prices between the two places is so great that those seeking profit will definitely continue to transport it, so that with one turn of the hand, profits will accumulate. This can be asserted.

Reasons for the US to Raise Silver Prices: The US government's raising of silver prices and buying of silver will inevitably lead anyone to speculate on its intentions. It is preparing for a second world war. Although the outcome of modern warfare ostensibly depends on the sharpness of firearms, it actually depends on economic power. Silver is more versatile than gold, and silver is more useful during wartime than in peacetime. European countries all use gold standards. During the European War, because it was difficult to purchase goods with gold coins, silver was purchased after the outbreak of the war, causing the price of silver to rise to 90 pence at that time. The brewing of a second world war is almost like the eve of the European War, with a sense of imminent outbreak. The US authorities, in view of the usefulness of silver, which is sufficient to determine the outcome of war, are raising the price of silver and buying silver to prepare in advance. This is common knowledge to discerning people, and silver-using countries in the Far East, such as our country, are exporting large quantities.

The Relationship Between Silver Price Fluctuations is Extremely Important: He continued, the level of silver prices is of great importance to the whole world and cannot be viewed as merely a matter of commercial conditions. Therefore, the current US increase in silver prices and buying of silver is no different from the silver price increase during the European War. Observing the outbreak of the European War in 1914, the belligerent countries, not knowing the importance of silver, collected cash from each other, causing the price of silver to fall to 22 and one-eighth pence. After the start of the war, they realized the relationship between silver and war, and the price of silver gradually soared to 90 pence one year after the armistice. From this, we can further believe in the intention of raising the price of silver and buying silver. Mr. Qiu also listed the following facts about the relationship between silver price fluctuations and the reasons for changes:

Year Highest Price (Pence) Lowest Price (Pence) Reason

1897 29.13 23.12 Japan adopts the gold standard, Greco-Turkish War

1900 30.13 27. Chinese Boxer Rebellion, South African War, India large minting of Rupees

1902 26.2 21.1 Silver market falls sharply, end of South African War, unstable Chinese trade due to unresolved Boxer indemnities

1904 28.9 24.7 Russo-Japanese War, Mexican currency reform, Indian silver purchases

1906 33.2 29. India large purchases of silver coins, US government begins buying silver

1907 32.7 24.3 India stops buying silver, silver prices fall sharply, US panic, Bank of England interest rates raised to 7%

1911 26.2 23.2 Strikes in the United States, Chinese Revolution

1913 29.6 26.2 Establishment of Chinese foreign debt of 25 million pounds, India buys 5.5 million pounds of silver

1914 27.12 22.2 Outbreak of the Great War, major changes in financial and stock markets, Britain large minting of silver coins

1917 55. 35.11 Continuation of the European War, countries minting silver coins, silver market soared, to 90 pence one year after the armistice

Cotton Association Submits Document to the Yuan, Departments, and Committees 132

To Change the Standards for Eliminating Moisture and Impurities in Cotton

The Chinese Cotton Industry Association submitted a document to the Central Political Committee, the National Government, the Executive Yuan, the Legislative Yuan, the Ministry of Industry, and the Cotton Control Committee, stating that the association's members are all cotton merchants in our country and have close ties with the production and sales of Chinese cotton. They have always tried their best to support improvement matters. However, it seems that careful consideration and overall planning should be made in advance before implementing reforms. Once implemented, they can be carried out unimpeded. The promulgation of the Regulations on Eliminating Water and Impurities in Cotton shows the government's determination to improve, and the association welcomes it without hesitation. However, after examining the articles and the actual situation in various places, there are slight differences. For the sake of the safety and future of all cotton merchants, the association cannot remain silent and offers its humble opinions, hoping that they will be examined separately to reassure businesses. Article 2 of the Regulations on Eliminating Water and Impurities in Cotton states, "The maximum limit for moisture content in domestic cotton sold on the market is 13%." Cotton material is fluffy and easily absorbs moisture. According to the regulations, this may be suitable for dry cotton-producing areas in the northern plateau, but the climate in the south is humid. In the cotton-producing areas of the southern provinces, such as south of the Yellow River and the Yangtze River Basin, the natural moisture content will inevitably be above 13% for several months during the new cotton production season. Then, due to climate and geographical reasons, the natural moisture content is beyond human control and cannot actually meet the requirements of these regulations. What kind of grievances will merchants and people suffer if they are subject to legal restrictions or criminal penalties as a result? Therefore, it is requested to make slight changes. It is proposed that from the beginning of the new cotton production season to the end of December of this year, the maximum limit be temporarily set at 14%. This is the first request. Furthermore, Article 8 of the same regulations states, "For cotton sold on a forward or spot basis, if the cottonseeds and other impurities exceed the standards of both parties or the publicly set standards by more than 0.05%, the sale and use of the cotton should be stopped." In addition to cottonseeds, the so-called impurities include cottonseed, seed flowers, broken leaves, and sand. These also resemble natural impurities. Because the cotton gins used in our country are different from those in the United States and India, it is inevitable that cottonseeds will jump in during ginning. As for cottonseed, broken leaves, and sand, it is impossible to extract them completely due to work and time constraints. This is also a fact. For the convenience of both buyers and sellers, it is proposed that the total weight of Chinese cotton containing cottonseed, seed flowers, broken leaves, and sand be temporarily set at 0.05% as the legal standard, with no increase or deduction, and 2% as the "publicly set standard." Cotton containing cottonseed, seed flowers, broken leaves, and sand exceeding 0.05% up to 2% will be deducted, and cotton exceeding the publicly set standard should be stopped from sale and use. In addition to the above items, any other kind of false quality should be strictly prohibited. Once discovered, it should be regarded as unqualified. This is the second request. Furthermore, the association has further requests. The regulations on impurity inspection methods have not yet been specified. Whether the inspection procedures apply technical scientific methods and how they will be handled should be announced for compliance. In short, the principle of eliminating water and impurities in cotton is welcomed by cotton merchants. However, there are difficulties in some aspects, and the actual difficulties must be truthfully presented for slight changes to be made, so as to achieve the effect of eliminating fraud, relieve the cotton merchants' difficulties, and whether it is feasible. This matter is hereby submitted for review, and it is hoped that it will be accepted with understanding, which would be a great kindness.

Xiamen Chamber of Commerce 134

Requests Release of Detained Zhang Rice by Telegram

Xiamen telegram, Shen Bao forwards to all administrative agencies and people's organizations for your consideration: According to the Shanghai rice merchants from Xiamen, the tens of thousands of bags of Zhang rice applied for by our group are definitely domestic rice and have been inspected and released by the Xiamen Customs. However, some people in Shanghai are creating an atmosphere, saying that Japanese rice is being used as a substitute, hoping to monopolize and hoard, causing the Shanghai Customs to misunderstand and detain the rice. This is proof that abundance and scarcity are different. Moreover, Zhang rice and Japanese rice have different properties and can be easily distinguished, but now rumors are spreading from nowhere, with no factual basis, which is obviously someone being jealous and coming up with this malicious plan. Currently, the Zhang rice is still being detained by the Shanghai Customs, and it is required to pay six yuan per bag as a deposit. We request you to implement it as a gesture of gratitude, Xiamen Chamber of Commerce and Shanghai Rice Merchant Association, respectfully.

The Municipal Party Department Requests the Installation of Guard Posts and Streetlights

Such Equipment Cannot Be Delayed

The Shanghai Municipal Party Department, noting that the Bailianjing area of Pudong has become increasingly prosperous in recent times, but there are no guard posts or streetlights, specially wrote to the Municipal Government yesterday to instruct the Public Security Bureau and the Public Works Bureau to handle this matter. The original letter is recorded below: "Respectfully, we received a report from the Fifth District Executive Committee of our association, stating that the Second Branch of our district reported that the Hedong area of Bailianjing, Pudong, was originally a remote area, but since factories and warehouses have sprung up, the market has become increasingly prosperous, and the population has increased without end. However, there is still a lack of road facilities, such as streetlights, which are the most urgent need at present. It is now found that the roads from Bailianjing to Xinma Road and Liuli Bridge are all important thoroughfares, but they become a dark world at night, so that the public is often harmed by bandits and petty thieves. Recently, a Mr. Chen was kidnapped due to the darkness on the road, which allowed the bandits to escape. The construction of an alcohol factory has recently begun, and the area is even more lively, and the population is becoming more and more complex, with good and bad people difficult to distinguish. If equipment is not installed early, walking at night may result in bandit attacks. Therefore, detailed drawings of the street lighting routes have been prepared and submitted to your association for review, requesting that they be forwarded to the municipal government, ordering the Public Works Bureau and the Public Security Bureau to send personnel to survey the location, install streetlights, and add police officers to ensure public safety and avoid the increasingly fierce bandit atmosphere. Based on this, the application of the branch to install streetlights and add posts in the Hedong area of Bailianjing, Pudong, are important facilities for local security and are truly urgently needed. Based on the aforementioned situation, we have enclosed the route map and respectfully submit it to your association for review, and ask that you forward it to the municipal government, ordering the Public Works Bureau and the Public Security Bureau to handle it as soon as possible, so as to facilitate transportation and maintain security, which would be beneficial to the public. The attached route map is enclosed. Based on this, the corresponding original document is enclosed for your review and handling. Sincerely, Shanghai Municipal Government."

Jiangyou Poet Tao Xiaoliu Passes Away 140

According to the Central News Agency, Mr. Tao Xiaoliu of Nanchang, whose given name was Mu and also known as Bosun, was famous for his poetry in the Southern Society at the end of the Qing Dynasty. He traveled around all his life and had many friends at home and abroad. Some years ago, when Ye Chucang and Hu Puan took charge of the Jiangsu government, he once served as the magistrate of Nanhui, Taicang, and other counties, and was known for his integrity wherever he went. To this day, people in the counties still praise him. His family environment was extremely tragic throughout his life. After his wife died in middle age, he never remarried. His only son and daughter also passed away one after another. Alone, he only relied on his son-in-law for support. After the January 28th Incident, he declined officialdom and retired to Suzhou, living a simple and poor life, spending these tragic remaining years. Unexpectedly, this summer he contracted a minor illness and sought medical treatment, but it was ineffective. He eventually died on July 30th at No. 25 Jinshi Lane, Suzhou. After his death, his relatives could not be contacted. Only his son-in-law, Feng Yangru, took care of the funeral arrangements. The funeral will be held on September 2nd and he will be temporarily placed in the Changshan Bureau to await burial in Jiangxi. He left behind many poems and lyrics, which will also be compiled and published by his son-in-law.

Oil Tycoon Donates Land for Hospital 147

Zhongshan Hospital Construction Begins

New Buildings for National Medical College Also Break Ground

Entire Project Scheduled for Completion in 240 Days

Upon Completion, It Will Be the Most Advanced and Largest Hospital in the Far East

American oil tycoon Rockefeller has donated 150 acres of the former baseball field for the construction of China's most advanced and largest Zhongshan Hospital. With sufficient funding raised for the entire hospital, the project has been awarded to the Kee Tai Construction Company, and construction has commenced. The completion is scheduled for 240 days. Simultaneously, the new site for the National Medical College, with a budget of 300,000 yuan allocated by the Ministry of Education, has also broken ground along with the new headquarters of the National Medical Association. Yesterday, the reporter from the Shen Shi News Agency interviewed Mr. Yan Fuqing, the person in charge of the hospital, who provided the following details:

Construction Begins on Zhongshan Hospital: The entire site for Zhongshan Hospital, 150 acres of the former baseball field, was voluntarily donated by the American oil tycoon. As for the construction expenses, 700,000 yuan has been raised through donations, with over 400,000 yuan already collected and the remainder expected to be collected soon. The hospital project was awarded to the Kee Tai Construction Company on the 23rd of this month, and construction has commenced. The contract stipulates completion in 240 days, with the opening ceremony scheduled for June of next year. The hospital building will be entirely Western-style, constructed entirely of steel and concrete, with an extremely grand appearance.

Advanced and Comprehensive Internal Facilities: Upon completion, the hospital will be the most advanced and largest in China. The initial phase of construction includes 550 beds, with the capacity to accommodate 1,000 outpatients simultaneously. Upon completion of the future expansion, the capacity can be increased to 1,000 beds. The medical departments are divided as follows: A. Department of Internal Medicine: (1) Dermatology, (2) Pediatrics, (3) Cardiology and Pulmonology, (4) Neurology, (5) Preventive Medicine; B. Department of Surgery: (1) Orthopedics, (2) Urology; C. Department of Obstetrics; D. Specialty Departments: (1) Ophthalmology, (2) Otolaryngology, (3) Gynecology; E. Obstetrics and Gynecology; F. Urology and Reproductive Medicine. In addition, special facilities include: (1) Electrotherapy Room, (2) X-ray Room, (3) Radium Therapy Room, (4) Surgical Pathology Department, (5) Laboratory, (6) Pharmacy, (7) Pathology Research Room, (8) Physiotherapy Department. The entire hospital has four floors. The first and second floors partly house the treatment rooms and offices for each department, while the remainder and the entire third floor are for patient rooms. The fourth floor is for the treatment of children's diseases.

Seeking Overseas Donations of Medical Equipment: Because the funds raised for the construction of the hospital are still limited, efforts are being made to solicit voluntary donations of construction materials, such as steel and concrete, as well as various internal equipment, from relevant parties, in order to achieve maximum benefit at the lowest possible cost. As for the medical equipment, valued at over 100,000 yuan, fundraising is underway overseas. Currently, those who have donated 50,000 yuan or more include Madam Song, the Jianghai Customs, the Huangpu Conservancy Board, the Bankers Association, the Money Dealers Association, and Westerners Sir Elly Rodone and Sir Victor Sasoon. Those who have donated over 1,000 yuan include Liu Hongsheng, Yan Huiqing, Zhang Xingcun, the Yokohama Specie Bank, the Hongkong and Shanghai Banking Corporation, Madam Liu Chen Baozhen, Huang Zhendong, Yan Lailian, the Kailan Mining Administration Sales Office, Hu Mengjia, Kong Xiangxi, Du Yuesheng, and the British American Tobacco Company.

New Buildings for Medical College Also Under Construction: Of the entire baseball field site, in addition to the part used for the Zhongshan Hospital site, the remaining part will be used for the construction of new buildings for the Shanghai National Medical College. Construction has also commenced simultaneously and is expected to be completed at the same time as the Zhongshan Hospital. All 300,000 yuan in construction expenses have been allocated by the Ministry of Education upon request to the Executive Yuan. After the completion of the new buildings for the Medical College, the internal divisions will include both pre-medical and medical departments. The medical department will be further divided into seven departments: Anatomy, Physiology, Pathology, Pharmacology, Biology, Chemistry, and Bacteriology and Hygiene. Zhongshan Hospital will serve as the teaching hospital.

Recurrent Expenses Secured: According to Mr. Yan, in addition to the recurrent expenses already allocated for the Medical College, the recurrent expenses for Zhongshan Hospital will be covered by constructing residential buildings for rent on part of the remaining land, generating an annual income of 50,000 yuan. The remaining land will be rented to build the Hong Ying Library, the Chinese Medical Association's school building, and the Shanghai Tennis Club, with the rental income serving as the hospital's endowment fund. At the same time, all future doctors at Zhongshan Hospital will be concurrently employed by the existing doctors and professors at the National Medical College, saving a significant amount of expenditure. Furthermore, the income from future consultations should also be able to sustain the hospital. If there is a shortfall, it is planned to raise funds from various parties at any time.

Zheng Ruyi Invents 149

Scientific Building Materials

Recapturing Significant Interests

Nine out of ten building materials in our country are imported from abroad, and domestically produced ones are rare. According to Mr. Ji Zejin, Director of the Guidance Department of the International Trade Bureau, chemist Zheng Ruyi, recognizing this situation, established the Yale Manufacturing Factory three years ago, specializing in the production of various domestic building materials, hoping to recapture these interests. Currently, the output has increased to twelve types. The first two products to be launched, waterproofing paste and transparent waterproofing varnish, have eliminated the import of similar foreign goods and have had a significant impact on asphalt felt. The factory has three new products as follows:

Collox Oil: Cement roofs mostly use asphalt felt, which is not only expensive and labor-intensive but also black, uneven, and heavy. Collox Oil is a type of diluted chemical oil that only needs to be applied to the cement surface to penetrate and seal the micropores.

Waterproofing Varnish: Repairing leaking cement roofs is very difficult because cement mortar is ineffective. With the advent of waterproofing paste, this problem can be easily solved. Any type of leaking cement, tin, or asphalt felt roof or platform can be repaired with a single coat, which is very convenient.

Wood Preservative Oil: Wood Preservative Oil can make wood resistant to decay and durable. It can be used alone or mixed with tung oil. It is a preservative for wooden piles, boats, and building lumber. Its selling price is one-third lower than similar imported products on the market.

Madwoman Causes Uproar at American Consulate 150

Appears to be of Mixed Japanese-American Descent, Approximately Fifteen or Sixteen Years Old

Disrupted Operations for a Long Time, No Place to Send Her - Feeling the Hospital System is Inadequate

According to the "Great American Evening Post", at around ten o'clock this morning (the 25th), a girl who appeared to be of mixed Japanese-American descent, approximately fifteen or sixteen years old, entered the American Consulate General on Jiangxi Road through the main gate. She walked into the passport room on the lower floor and shouted loudly, overturned the counter, and sent ink bottles and other objects on the counter flying in all directions. The staff were caught off guard and did not know what to do. Once they regained their composure, the girl had already flown into the adjacent shipping affairs room, shouting wildly. Before they could raise a hand, she was seized by an employee. They then began to discuss how to handle the situation. The girl calmed down slightly, but the person holding her loosened their grip for a moment, and the girl ran wildly out of the room, up the back stairs. The staff chased closely behind. The girl reached the office upstairs and shouted wildly three times, encountering the American Consul General, Mr. Kirk, by chance. She abandoned Mr. Kirk's office and went straight to the corridor connecting the American Consulate Court and the office. She passed through the court clerk's office and ran wildly into a room connected to the office of the American Assessor, Mr. Hillmer. After knocking down a clock, she escaped to the balcony outside, where she was apprehended by the court's Deputy Bailiff, Mr. Peterson. At that time, the consulate staff had already called the Public Works Department's ambulance, which transported the girl to the General Hospital. The director refused to admit her because the hospital did not have a psychiatric department, so she was sent back to the American Consulate. The consulate staff then consulted with Mr. Zhong Si, the Director-General of the Public Works Department, by telephone. They learned that the Victoria Nursing Home could treat mental illnesses, but it was full and could not accommodate her. In the end, the girl was sent to the General Police Station, to be handled by Dr. Julien, the Director of the Health Department. The American Consulate was busy with work when it was disrupted by this madwoman, causing operations to be suspended for a long time. Moreover, there was no place to send this madwoman for a while. Therefore, there was much criticism of the Public Works Department's facilities, especially the ambulance system. The driver at the time, knowing that the General Hospital did not have a psychiatric department, had no choice but to transport her to the hospital. This was not the driver's fault. Until there was no other solution, she was sent to the General Police Station, barely resolving the matter. The deficiencies in Shanghai's hospital system are truly regrettable.

On Linping Road 151

A Young Woman is Assassinated

Mao Jinsheng is Highly Suspected

Jin Wubao, a 25-year-old woman from Pingwang, was married to Mr. Xiao Jin, a native of Shengze. However, Wubao did not abide by the traditional virtues of a married woman. Several years ago, in Shengze, she became acquainted with Mao Jinsheng, 32 years old, from Huzhou. Before long, she ran away from her husband and came to Shanghai to live with Mao in a rented room above a stove shop next to the Yuanxing Li on Yuezhou Road. At the same time, Mao Jinsheng became a driver at a silk factory, and Wubao also worked as a textile worker at a spinning mill. Their combined income was enough to provide them with a comfortable life. However, recently, Mao suddenly heard that Wubao had been engaging in illicit activities again. He questioned her about it the day before yesterday, but Wubao denied it vehemently. This led to an argument between them. In anger, Wubao stormed out of the house and went to stay temporarily with Madam Yu, the wife of Xu Yuhui, a carpenter at Tongshunxing Woodwork, No. 88 Linping Road. Yu and Wubao were close friends, so she was welcomed and given a bed in the attic. Yesterday morning, around five o'clock, Wubao got up and went downstairs to wash clothes by the water pipe. At the time, Madam Yu and her husband were still sound asleep. Suddenly, they were awakened by a scream that came from downstairs. They quickly put on their clothes and went downstairs to investigate, only to find Wubao lying on the ground, blood gushing from wounds all over her body. Her breath had stopped. Xu and others were extremely frightened and rushed to report to the Third Division of the Fifth District. The police station dispatched officers to investigate and discovered that Wubao had suffered seven knife wounds, all to vital areas. A murder weapon was found next to her body. The knife was bent, likely because the assailant used excessive force. The police immediately ordered the neighborhood head to report the case to the local court. Yesterday afternoon at three o'clock, a prosecutor was dispatched to conduct an inquest. He ordered the body to be temporarily coffined and stored, pending the arrest of the assailant. The Third Division of the Fifth District brought the murder weapon back to the station for safekeeping and summoned Xu Yuhui and Madam Yu to the station for questioning. They claimed that Mao Jinsheng was suspected of Wubao's death. Therefore, the police station ordered officers to secretly arrest him. However, Mao had already fled. The station immediately prepared a report to the General Bureau, which in turn ordered the Detective Brigade to pursue him.

Perfume and Cosmetics Worth Over One Million 152

Imported in Seven Months

An Increase of Over 40,000 Yuan Compared to the Same Period Last Year

Clear Evidence of the Ineffectiveness of the Women's National Products Year

According to the International Trade Bureau, the total value of perfumes and cosmetics imported from various countries since July of this year reached 1,006,140 yuan. Of this amount, 245,295 yuan was imported from France, 60,002 yuan from Germany, 148,845 yuan from the United Kingdom, 90,162 yuan from Hong Kong, 161,787 yuan from Japan, 309,119 yuan from the United States, and 2,595 yuan from other countries. This is an increase of 49,845 yuan compared to 956,295 yuan during the same period last year. The import value for July was 148,268 yuan, an increase of 4,224 yuan compared to June. At a time when international trade is declining and our country is promoting the Women's National Products Year, the import and export of various goods has decreased sharply. Only the import of perfumes and cosmetics has increased compared to last year, which is sufficient evidence of the ineffectiveness of promoting the Women's National Products Year.

Zhou Shengfa, Trafficking Red Pills 153

in North Station, Transferred to the Local Court

Previously Arrested Accomplices Have All Been Executed

Zhou Firmly Denies All Charges

On February 4th of this year, the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau uncovered a case of trafficking red pills at the North Railway Station, arresting Zhao Zuting and Wang Weicheng (aka Xiao Wang) and three police officers who protected and transported the drugs. They seized 2.4 million red pills. All arrested accomplices have been executed. However, Xiao Wang implicated Zhou Shengfa, residing at No. 20 Yuanyuan Li, Gordon Road, as an accomplice. Detective Lin Tianpeng of the Police Bureau, together with detectives from the Gordon Road Police Station, arrested Zhou and handed him over to the First Special Court for detention. The details have been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Wu Tingqi continued the hearing in the Eighth Criminal Court. Zhou Shengfa hired Jiang Yiping and Fan Gang as lawyers to defend him. After the Police Station's lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, stated the case, Detective Lin presented a document containing Wang Weicheng's confession, requesting the court to prohibit the defendant's lawyers from viewing it. Lawyer Jiang immediately objected, stating that, according to the law, the defense lawyers have the right to examine evidence related to the defendant. If it is unrelated to the defendant, they can be exempted from viewing it. Attorney Zhan Jifeng, the legal advisor of the Police Bureau, also appeared in court requesting transfer, stating that according to the agreement, when inland courts transfer suspects to the concession courts, if the identity of the suspect is confirmed, they should be transferred immediately. If it is another government agency, they must also submit evidence of the crime. The Police Bureau's application to transfer the suspect Zhou Shengfa has sufficient proof of the suspect's identity and the crime. The suspect should be handed over to the officers of the Police Bureau to be taken back for investigation. Zhou Shengfa completely denied all charges, stating that he did not know Wang and Zhao and was not aware of the manufacturing of red pills and would not dare to do so. In the end, the court ruled that Zhou Shengfa should be transferred to the Shanghai Local Court Prosecutor's Office for investigation. The evidence and files were returned in court.

Many Storms in the Sea of Love 154

Russian Woman Shoots French Lover

Due to Monetary Disputes, the Two Parties Become Irreconcilable

Russian Woman Arrested, French Lover Pleads on Her Behalf

- Russian Woman Released on 1,000 Yuan Bail, Rescheduled Hearing -

Suslovva Kordia, a 26-year-old Russian woman, wife of a German aviator, living at No. 12 Talas Road, French Concession, is beautiful and has some savings. She is romantic and met Ladolai, a French man living at No. 698 Rue Pétain, two years ago, and they fell in love. Ladolai, 29 years old, originally opened a restaurant, but closed due to poor business. He then resided at Suslovva Kordia's house and owed six months of rent. Suslovva asked Ladolai to pay, but Ladolai was unable to do so, and the love between the two gradually cooled. Ladolai also owed a food store on Route Mercier eight yuan, which Suslovva guaranteed. The day before yesterday, Suslovva suddenly withdrew the guarantee, asking the store to claim directly from Ladolai. The two parties became antagonistic because of these monetary issues. On the 8th of this month, Suslovva evicted Ladolai. That night, Ladolai went to Suslovva's house, climbed up to the window, reached through the window, and slapped Suslovva in the face. At that time, Suslovva told Ladolai that if he came to make trouble again, she would use a gun. At the same time, Suslovva reported the incident to the French police station, requesting protection. Yesterday morning at eleven o'clock, the Russian restaurant on Route Mercier sent someone to Ladolai to demand the eight yuan food bill. Suslovva then telephoned Ladolai and asked him to pay the restaurant bill immediately. Therefore, Ladolai went to Suslovva's house at three o'clock in the afternoon, and the two parties had a major conflict over the restaurant bill. Suslovva turned and went into the room, took out a pistol, and threatened Ladolai. Unexpectedly, the gun went off, and the bullet flew out. Ladolai dodged quickly, narrowly escaping. At that moment, a French officer living upstairs heard the gunshot and went downstairs to investigate. He caught up and snatched the pistol from Suslovva. Suslovva saw that the officer also had a pistol on his belt. Her pistol had just been taken away by the officer, but she reached for the officer's pistol, intending to commit suicide. The officer caught up again and snatched it away. He immediately telephoned the French police station, which dispatched a Western detective to take Suslovva to the police station. Yesterday noon, she was transferred to the First Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court, and Chief Judge Wang Gangxu interrogated her. Police lawyer Fei Xizhen stated the case and charged her with attempted murder. Then, Western detective Ivanoff, who handled the case, reported on the arrest of the defendant and the investigation. Ladolai, the plaintiff, stated that he had been in love with the defendant for two years. Yesterday, the defendant used a pistol to threaten him but had no intention of killing him. He asked the court to release her, stating that he did not want to sue her now. When the court questioned the defendant, she became incoherent and fainted. Ladolai immediately went forward to pick up Suslovva, comforting her in every way, and asked the court to release her, saying that he was willing to go to jail for her. Then, the defendant's lawyer, Ai Zhenlin, requested that she be allowed to be released on bail pending the rescheduled hearing. The court obtained the consent of the police and ordered the defendant to be released on 1,000 yuan bail, with the rescheduled hearing set for the 30th of this month.

New Sodium Vapor Lights 159

Shine Brightly on Gordon Road Last Night

The Light is Slightly Yellow, Passersby Stop and Stare in Surprise

According to the Datong News Agency, the Shanghai Electric Power Company recently plans to install a new type of street light with a longer range. According to the Datong News Agency reporter, the company's Chinese engineer revealed that the new street light uses sodium gas in a vacuum tube to emit light and is translated as Philora Sodium Lamp. Each sodium gas lamp can save a lot of electricity compared to ordinary street lights (ie, arc lamps), and the range of the light is also longer. The company has dispatched a large number of workers to rush to install the lights on Gordon Road (from Jing'an Temple Road to Avenue Haig). Seven or eight lights have been installed and tested last night. Compared with other ordinary street lights, the light is slightly yellow and exceptionally bright, causing those passing by to stop and stare in surprise. According to the Datong News Agency reporter, this sodium gas lamp is good, but the cost of each material needs to reach more than one hundred and fifty yuan, while the ordinary street lights currently used on the roads cost only more than ten yuan per lamp, which is too expensive and may exceed the Public Works Department's budget.

Guangfu Road 160

Apprentice at Yongshun Rice Shop Dies by Hanging

Why Was Sudden Illness Falsely Reported as Cause of Death?

Yesterday at 5:30 PM, the Public Security Bureau of the Fourth District of Zhabei received a phone call reporting that an apprentice at Yongshun Rice Shop, No. 385, west of Xinzha Bridge on Guangfu Road, was suffering from a sudden illness. The district immediately relayed the call to the Firefighting Joint Association, dispatching an ambulance. Upon arrival at the rice shop, it was discovered that the apprentice was not suffering from a sudden illness but had died by hanging on the drying platform. The Firefighting Association then called the Fourth District again. District Chief Gong, noting the discrepancy between the initial report of sudden illness and the Firefighting Association's report of death by hanging, considered the case suspicious. He dispatched police officer Wu Dichen to investigate. He found the apprentice kneeling on the drying platform, with several shop assistants attempting to rescue him, but the apprentice had already died. The deceased was wearing a singlet, white cotton pants, and gray socks, with a flat-top haircut. The owner of the rice shop, Yisheng, was also brought to the district for questioning. He stated that the apprentice's name was Wang Bogen, 19 years old, from Wusong, and had been working at the shop for four years, having completed his apprenticeship. Today (i.e., yesterday) was payday; the deceased earned seven yuan per month and had already received his wages. He did not know why he committed suicide. There were over ten other apprentices in the shop, as well as over ten accountants and senior staff members. After reviewing the statements, the official, considering the case a matter of life and death, reported it to the Public Security Bureau's Inspectorate and ordered the local bailiff to report it to the Shanghai Local Court for a coroner's inquest.

Special Article

Exhortation to Venerate Confucius 173

By Wu Tiecheng

--The Significance of Commemorating the Former Teacher Confucius--

Recently, the Central Government has designated August 27th, Confucius's birthday, as a memorial day for the Most Sage and Former Teacher Confucius, to commemorate Confucius's noble and great personality, to elucidate Confucius's broad and profound learning, to invigorate the weak and frivolous minds of the people, and to save the culture that is about to be cut off. On this holy birthday, our national populace, carrying on the past and opening up the future, should deeply reflect on how to encourage and continue the legacy of the Former Teacher Confucius, and take on the historical mission of everyone. I hereby reveal several meanings to express the author's admiration.

In recent years, trendy and frivolous people in the country have often belittled Confucius's teachings, selectively quoting and arbitrarily distorting them, believing that they do not meet the needs of the times, even laughing, scolding, and wantonly insulting Confucius's personality. The truth that fills the universe has absolutely no absolute temporality, only true objective sociality. The survival of a nation also has its unshakeable foundation, which is history and culture. Therefore, although Premier Sun Yat-sen advocated a radical revolution, he not only did not destroy the foundation upon which the nation relied for its livelihood, but also cherished it for fear of not doing enough. Therefore, in Premier Sun Yat-sen's lectures on the principle of national revival, he said that we must restore the nation's self-confidence, and we must restore and promote the spirit of our country's inherent culture. This is the first basic understanding that we should have when commemorating Confucius today.

Examining the development of modern Western culture and the strength of national power, it all originates from the "Renaissance" (La Renaissance). The driving force of the Renaissance was the Greek thought that had been flowing underground for thousands of years. European history, viewed through the lens of culture, has two major sources: one is Greek thought and the other is Christian thought. The former is characterized by physical and instinctive, self-awareness, liberalism, the present world, human-centrism, self-satisfaction, naturalism, intellectual, artistic, scientific skepticism, empiricism, and objective tendencies. The latter is characterized by spiritual and ascetic, knowledge of God, absolute obedience, clericalism, the kingdom of heaven, theocentrism, altruism, supernaturalism, religious, moral, faith, dogmatism, and subjective tendencies. Greek thought originated more than 2,600 years ago, and was most developed during the time of Pericles in Athens, when reason and emotion could each find their balance. As Athens declined, Rome succeeded it, and it transformed into extreme selfish hedonism. Licentiousness, extravagance, and cruelty prevailed. Christian thought, to remedy these shortcomings and correct these deviations, arose in response. Although Christ died for his faith, the religion flourished greatly after three or four hundred years. However, once a single authority was established, abuses arose again. Monks monopolized knowledge to keep the people ignorant, clinging to the end of rituals and ceremonies, and losing their fundamental spirit. At that time, people became slaves of the monks. This created what historians call the "Dark Ages of the Middle Ages." At this time, the Greek thought that had been flowing underground for thousands of years rose up again, with a new look, emphasizing reason, valuing nature, and creating the development of modern science; respecting individuality, valuing freedom, and promoting the development of modern Western politics and society. From this, it can be seen that if an idea loses its true meaning, it will inevitably lead to abuses; if used properly, it can promote the evolution of society. It is not changed its value because of ancient and modern, new and old. This is the second basic understanding that we should have when commemorating Confucius today.

In the past history of China, successive dynasties hung up the banner of respecting Confucius, but in reality, it was Lao Tzu, not Confucius, that dominated the thinking of the Chinese people. Since the Han Dynasty, the style of learning had greatly deteriorated. The thoughts of various schools were suppressed, and the theory of investigating things to extend knowledge was even despised. The intellectual class, frustrated by the unpredictability of emperors and the unattainability of wealth and status, embraced the principles of purity and inaction, and adopted an attitude of patience and retreat, thereby creating a decadent individualism and a lazy romanticism. The scholars of the Han Dynasty emphasized the study of textual criticism. The scholars of the Jin, Wei, and Six Dynasties advocated the style of Huang-Lao and pure conversation. Later, the Tang Dynasty valued commentaries, the Song Dynasty valued Neo-Confucianism, the Ming Dynasty valued the Eight-legged essay, and the Qing Dynasty valued textual research. All of these failed to recognize the true meaning of Confucianism. Discussing metaphysics and practicing quietism became increasingly empty. Being obsessed with fame and fortune did nothing to improve the country and society. The decadent trend further formed a great social inertia, completely eliminating the active ability and enterprising spirit of the general public. After thousands of years of long history, our Chinese nation, whether in science, art, life, or in the methods and abilities of organizing society and establishing a country, has shown a phenomenon of decline and has not made significant progress. Therefore, if we want to seek the reasons for the decline of our nation today, we should not blame Confucius, but we should deeply regret the loss of the true meaning of Confucianism. This is the third basic understanding that we should have when commemorating Confucius today.

Confucius's knowledge is profound and broad, and this short article cannot describe even a fraction of it. However, Confucius's contribution to creating our national culture cannot be denied by any fair historian. The Chinese nation, in the time of Yao, Shun, Yu, Tang, Wen, Wu, and the Duke of Zhou, can be said to have been a very glorious era. Yao, Shun, Yu, Tang, Wen, Wu, and the Duke of Zhou all understood the principles and methods of building a country and organizing society. They were able to strive to create social and national systems in practice and gradually seek their improvement, thereby laying the foundation for the evolution of Chinese society. However, at that time, academic culture was very scattered. Although the Duke of Zhou created a model by formulating rituals and music, academic books were still stored in the palace and had not yet been popularized or democratized. Confucius was able to inherit the merits of Yao, Shun, Yu, Tang, Wen, Wu, and the Duke of Zhou, and sort out, promote, and develop the various cultural relics and systems of that time, making them academic, systematic, popular, and democratic. He collected the great achievements of learning at that time. Confucius revived the spirit of "teaching tirelessly," based on the principles of the former kings' organization of the country and management of society, and then trained the public, influencing the public, and making the public understand the responsibilities they should bear to the country and society. Furthermore, based on the principles of extending knowledge through the investigation of things, making one's will sincere, rectifying one's heart, cultivating one's person, regulating one's family, governing one's state, and bringing peace to all under heaven, he established the foundation of our country's natural sciences, social sciences, ethics, and politics. This talent and merit in promoting culture and creating learning is especially worthy of admiration for all ages. This is the fourth basic understanding that we should have when commemorating Confucius today.

Since the New Culture Movement, the biggest reason why people criticized Confucius was the so-called "cannibalistic ethics." In fact, we still need to evaluate the true meaning and function of rites. "Rites are the reality of righteousness and the discipline of the public. Rites are based on human behavior and are used to regulate the people." (All of the above are from the Book of Rites) Zhu Xi explained rites as the manifestations of heavenly principles and the rules of human affairs. The "origin" of rites is based on human nature, which is the so-called manifestations of heavenly principles. The use of rites is manifested in everything and is omnipresent, which is the rules of human affairs. The former is immutable, while the latter can be adjusted according to the times. Therefore, it is said that the Five Emperors had different rites, and that Confucius was a sage who adapted to the times. Those who advocate overthrowing ethics now do not know its original meaning and its use, thinking that it hinders the evolution of society. However, they do not know that rites can be changed with the times. Therefore, when discussing the reasons for the slow progress of Chinese society, we cannot blame rites, but only the misunderstanding and misuse of rites. Moreover, the relationship between rites and law is particularly close. Confucianism believes that the power of habit to control society is very great. If habits cannot be improved, all good laws and intentions will be in vain. The profound meaning of Confucianism's advocacy of the rule of rites is to make "everyone have the conduct of a gentleman." Legalists say, "Do not blame the people who are good by themselves." Confucianism is the opposite of them, believing that without "self-good people," good politics cannot appear. The fundamental spirit of Confucian political theory is that everyone in the country should be educated and become "self-good people," taking the cultivation of national personality as the primary meaning in politics. To seek rites from the complicated formalities is not only to underestimate Confucianism, but simply to misunderstand the true meaning of rites (see Liang Qichao's Pre-Qin Political Thought). Since the Xinhai Revolution in China, all good laws and systems have been tragically defeated. The way to save the situation now is to start with cultivating habits that are compatible with the rule of law. Premier Sun Yat-sen, based on his practical political experience, divided the steps of national construction into three stages: military rule, tutelage, and constitutional rule. The so-called tutelage is a preparatory work for promoting the rule of law. Recently, in view of the failure of all political revolutions over the years, the New Life Movement has emerged. The function of the New Life Movement is to transform the national psychology and life, to cultivate a life and habits that are compatible with the new society ruled by law. The basic principles of the New Life Movement are "propriety, righteousness, integrity, and a sense of shame." From this, it can be seen that Confucius's ethics are suitable for the current needs of Chinese society. This is the fifth basic understanding that we should have when commemorating Confucius today.

Mr. Liang Qichao once said in his lecture criticizing Hu Shih's Outline of the History of Chinese Philosophy, "I still remember the phrase 'specially beating the Confucius shop.' I think that such idle words should be said less. When debating issues, one should not give in. One should always show due respect to the personality of the other side. If one laughs, scolds, and curses, one will reduce the value of one's own words. One should be so respectful even to contemporaries, let alone to the ancients who have been kind to society." People today are too fashionable and often like to cater to the shallow psychology of society, creating novelty and innovation, regardless of whether it is suitable for national conditions, thereby hindering the development of truth and causing endless harm to the country and society. It is hoped that the people of the country can reflect on and correct this common problem so as not to fail the country's good intentions in commemorating Confucius. August 25, 23rd year.

Reading and Answers

Re-discussing the Chicken and Egg Problem (Continued) 174

--Reply to Hu Jie and Others

Regarding these endless cyclical questions, if we only pay attention to the phenomena we see before us, and only use the phenomena before us to argue, it is absolutely impossible to resolve them. This is because all present events are the result of the development of many past events, and all things have long historical roots. If we only see the current phenomena and do not pay attention to the historical development, then we will not know the source of this phenomenon. If we do not find the true source historically, but instead engage in empty talk about the current cyclical phenomena, then even if we argue for thousands of years, we will not be able to determine who the chicken and the egg belong to. Mr. Wang Zaifu mentioned in his letter that there is someone who advocates that the egg came before the chicken, his reason being that "every egg can hatch a chicken, but every chicken cannot necessarily lay an egg (because half of them are roosters), so it should be the egg that produces the chicken, not the chicken that produces the egg." This kind of statement is precisely a joke arising from only paying attention to the immediate reason and not paying attention to the historical origin. When we observe anything, we must look at it from the perspective of its development. In our previous discussion on the chicken and egg problem, we explained it from the perspective of biological development. We said that the phenomenon of laying eggs is a phenomenon that only occurs after the development of organisms to the multicellular stage. Before multicellular animals were formed, the act of laying eggs would not occur, so initially, it was multicellular animals that laid eggs, not eggs that gave birth to multicellular animals. In other words, it is the chicken that produces the egg (because the chicken represents multicellularity), not the egg that produces the chicken (because the egg is just an ovum).

Regarding other similar cyclical problems, we also need to explore their historical roots. For example, the question of human thought and the social environment: sometimes human thought can influence the environment, and sometimes the environment can determine human thought. Is it thought that determines the environment, or is it the environment that determines thought? This becomes another unsolvable problem. The French mechanical materialists of the eighteenth century fell into this kind of circular argument and could not find a way out. They admitted that the environment could determine human reason, and at the same time admitted that reason could change the world. They could not find a way out because they did not know how to study the historical roots of reason and society. However, we now know to study the development of society from the economic and material foundation, so we can now undoubtedly determine that the social environment determines people's thoughts first. Then the two influence each other.

Regarding the previously mentioned problem of the individual supporting the family and the family supporting the individual, or the mutual relationship between the individual and the boarding house owner, we will not discuss it for the time being. Please, readers, study it themselves and consider how to solve it. It would be best if readers could write their opinions to us, and then we will provide a practical answer.
