The lotus pod is like a honeycomb; in each room, a lotus seed can be peeled out, which is very delicious. So we went to pick them.

Steamships 242

— Bingyu

Question: "Why can a very heavy steamship float on the water and not sink?" Answer: "Let's look at an empty tin can from canned food. If you throw it into the water, does it float?" This question and answer were discussed between Wilson, the young owner of an iron shop in England, and his friend. Wilson said, "Iron ships can float on the water." The friend said, "Why does a piece of iron sink when you put it in the water?" Wilson, coming from an iron shop, used light iron plates to build a ship, 20 meters long and 1.5 meters wide, unlike the wooden ships of the past. Later, this ship lasted for seventy years. Since Wilson created iron ships that could float on water, imitators increased day by day. In 1820, Mengpi used an 80-horsepower steam engine to build an iron ship 40 meters long and 6 meters wide. After that, it was recognized that iron ships were stronger than wooden ships and would not sink. But what is the reason for floating on the water? I will explain it with buoyancy. For example, if you put a one-pound stone into the water, the weight of the stone is reduced by one pound due to the displacement of water. If you put part of the stone into the water, the submerged part is also reduced in weight by the same amount due to the pressure of the water. This principle was discovered by the Englishman Archimedes, which is the so-called effect of buoyancy. Because when a stone is put into the water, the stone is subjected to pressure from all directions, up, down, left, and right. The pressure from the left and right is the same, but the pressure from the top and bottom is different. That is, the upward force from below is stronger than the weight of the water displaced by the stone. Therefore, anything that can float on the water is due to the effect of buoyancy. Because the weight of the object is lighter than the weight of the same volume of water, the weight is smaller than the buoyancy, and it will naturally float. The displacement of a steamship or warship is lighter than the steamship or warship itself, so it will naturally not sink. In other words, the total weight of the steamship (including cargo, passengers, and everything else), compared to the weight of the same volume of water, is lighter, so it floats. Therefore, when building steamships of tens of millions of tons, the amount of water displaced by the ship must be calculated first to determine how much weight can be loaded.

Shen Bao Local Supplement Amateur Weekly

On Order and Life 243

— Antian

What is order? Before discussing this topic, we must first give a simple definition. Order is having hierarchy and no chaos. In other words, it is a perfect set of rules that we, as living humans, need when handling our daily lives, so that it does not become reversed or inappropriate. From this, it can be seen that order is related to life—for people in any class.

At first glance, order is just two ordinary words that can be seen and heard everywhere, as common as eating and talking. However, we must not ignore it just because it is ordinary. I believe that if you discard this misconception and treat it like a newly invented thing, and put some effort into studying it, it will bring you great benefits; even the smallest condition can make you feel that things are going smoothly and that time is being saved. If you are someone who has paid attention to order, then you must be very familiar with these and feel that what I am saying is not false.

In the past, the person who understood the word order most thoroughly was probably Xiao E. He once said something very good about order: "When he gets up in the morning, he plans a way to handle the day, and then follows this order to do it; in this way, it is as if the person is holding a guide wire. Because only by following this wire can it lead you out of this maze of busyness. If a person can manage time in an orderly manner, then that person will have a ray of light in all undertakings; if there is no plan for order before doing things, it is just wasting time groping blindly. In this way, all kinds of difficulties will inevitably arise, and the clues will be complicated, making it difficult to control and even more difficult to inspect." McCauley also said: "Without method, no matter how good the undertaking, it will be difficult to succeed." When Webster edited his dictionary, it took him thirty-six years, but he later said to people: "My method and order have saved me at least ten or twenty years of time, and spared me a lot of worry and hard work." Judging from the words of the famous people above, having order in doing things is indeed a beneficial thing.

In fact, the benefits of this order are not limited to celebrities; they have the same great benefits for us. Here, we can give two examples at random. For example, in a large company, when there are many customers, if you don't follow the order to do things, in the end, you may give too much goods or collect too little money. Imagine! How annoyed you will feel at that time! Also, a housewife must have order if she wants to have a clean and lovely family. If not, if a guest comes, she will be busy wiping the table and sweeping the floor first, and then send someone to make tea and buy cigarettes when the guest is about to leave. How will this disorderly attitude of "sweeping the floor when the guest arrives and brewing tea when the guest leaves" make people feel the chaos of the family and the incompetence of the housewife! However, if we try to reverse this disorderly attitude, how comfortable will we feel!

Speaking of the development of this orderly attitude, it is naturally not something that can be learned in a day or two. It requires training in daily life, and it also requires using the brain to understand the importance and unimportance of things, and then determine the order of doing things. If you add training in this way, and once it becomes a habit, there will be no difficulty.

In conclusion, although the two words order seem too ordinary, if you can use them properly, it can not only reduce the waste of time, the trouble of doing things inappropriately, and increase the effectiveness of doing things, but also receive praise from others for your orderly work and your capable and promising person, and receive respect from others. At the same time, the progress and success of your career may benefit from these two ordinary words "order."

Outlying Postal Agency

Yixing Correspondence 244

— Kaihe, Wangli, Yixing County

It hasn't rained in Yixing for more than three months. The sun bakes in the sky like a fireball, and the intense heat evaporates the moisture deep in the ground. The weeds on the ground are withered and only a few thick roots remain; the sky is often filled with swarms of red dragonflies flying around in confusion. "Red dragonflies, flying in swarms; like red clouds, drought—drought—killing people!" The children sang while slapping bamboo branches.

There are unusually few pedestrians on the street. Only a group of shirtless people are piled up opposite the "Le Ye" tea shop, looking up and tiptoeing to look at the yellow paper and black characters posted on the wall. Some people are very serious about reading it out word by word:

"It is hereby decided that starting from the 13th of this month (i.e., June 2nd of the lunar calendar), the digging of the Wu River will commence. All workers must bring hoes, iron shovels, and other tools to the township office to collect work permits before 5:00 a.m. when the gong is sounded as a signal. This announcement.

Yixing Tang Zhuang Township Xueqiao Township Office"

The Wu River surrounding Tang Town—this is the widest river in the countryside, and it is also the main river that bears the dual mission of transportation and irrigation. The water from seventy-two mountain streams converges here to discharge, and the downstream flows into Yixing's famous "West Jiu" and then into Taihu Lake. It is not easy to dry up under normal drought conditions. On the contrary, if there are four or five inches of torrential rain during the plum rain season, it will flood because it cannot be discharged in time, washing away the thatched sheds. Now, under the most severe drought in the past sixty or seventy years, some parts of this river have cracks like turtle shells, and people are walking around in the riverbed. There are still a few places with stagnant water, but they are like the old phlegm in the throat of a consumptive patient, flowing sluggishly, telling people that this flow will not last long.

Since the yellow paper notice was posted, the quiet and dull air in the town has been mixed with noisy shouts for the past two days.

"The river is being dug! The river is being dug!" Ignorant children sang happily like ballads.

Most of the old women expressed a kind of sad complaint: People don't even have food to eat, so what are they digging the river for! The county has issued so much money for digging the river, it could also be used to save us poor people. If we are sincere and go to the "Meng Jiang Temple" to pray and burn more incense, that will be enough. The Bodhisattva is efficacious, and it will always rain.

The old farmers frowned with deep sorrow and just sighed there. They seemed to feel a kind of half-dead weariness towards this past life, and they did not have the courage to make a clearer imagination about the new life in the future. Sometimes, they even thought about "People's hearts are so cunning that there has been either drought or flood for years. If Heaven wants to destroy people, how can people be saved?"

Watching the withered crops, their hearts were boiling like oil pots, and they were so anxious that they had nowhere to go. Generally, those who rely on short-term work and busy work for a living have the strength but no place to sell it, so they have to lie softly on the bed with empty stomachs. Even if there is a little wheat left over from silkworms hidden in the jar (during the silkworm season, green wheat is mortgaged at a very low price for mulberry leaves to feed the silkworms; later, the silkworms were not raised, or they were raised but could not be sold at a price, so some wheat was completely eaten by the silkworms), such a drought would make life a problem. Some were so anxious that they had no choice but to start staging tragic scenes of the whole family committing suicide.

On the morning of the 13th, the urgent sound of gongs, clang, clang, clang, urged groups of farmers to go to the front of the township office. They squeezed together in an open space, expecting the allocation of work, and stretched their necks, looking at the closed gate of the township office.

The door opened with a creak, and they crowded forward a little more. What particularly caught their attention was the work permit made of white bamboo cloth and the self-ringing clock hanging on the wall indicating 5:30, because they were afraid that they would not receive the work permit if they were late.

Dang...dang, it was exactly six o'clock: there were still many farmers left in the yard.

"Those who have not received a work permit, come earlier tomorrow!" The township head reported and went in according to the rules they had set—

Page 22

One hundred and fifty people are full, and work starts at six o'clock.

Those who were squeezed out of the work circle burst into a riot in the flickering of the morning light, but who cared? After a while, they could only disperse in frustration.

In a wide and long riverbed, white lime lines have been drawn, dividing it into blocks. They took off their clothes and found their positions one by one; one person took a hoe and a basket to dig the soil, and another person transported the dug-out soil and poured it on both sides of the river bank. In the cool morning, the work was very vigorous. Soon, the wet soil had piled up on both sides of the river.

The heat of the sun pressed directly on the ground. The low-lying river ditch was filled with more than one hundred and fifty naked, purple-copper-skinned farmers, each bending over and gritting their teeth, digging at the solid mud that had been pressed by the water. The pearl-like sweat, the rapid breathing, the skin that gradually turned from black to purple, contrasted with the swinging hoes and the bright iron chisels, all presented an exhibition of "human flesh" and "strength."

At this time, a thin layer of turbid mud in the riverbed, clumps of residual algae, and many dead small fish and shrimp were fermented by the sun, constantly emitting a foul odor. Most of the supervisors had already fled. They were suffocated and could not breathe, so they had to run to the willow trees by the river, stretch their sore backs; but the mischievous hairy caterpillars on the trees would give them a hot and itchy pain. Some simply sat on the handle of their hoes or iron shovels, braving the heat of the sun, smoking yellow cigarettes, and clearing the stuffiness accumulated in their chests.

But such rest would be reported. At that time, the supervisors would run over with a stern face, and they would have to return to the oil pot-like riverbed one by one. Some were so hot that they had no choice but to roll around in the mud.

The sweat on their bodies was almost gone. The dryness of the throat and the hunger of the body forced them to grab the clear well water carried by passers-by to drink. In summer, they would not have so much tea to drink, and well water became the most common natural drink in the countryside.

When they saw someone dig up a bottle or a fishing fork that had fallen into the water from a fishing boat, many lines of sight would immediately focus on it; everyone fantasized that there would be these things or more valuable gold, silver, pearls, and treasures under the hoe, so sometimes they would work even more excitedly. However, such fantasies would fade away like the sun and eventually disappoint them.

The sound of the gong, clang, clang, clang, rang out with the setting sun, announcing that the day's work was over. So they dragged their tired bodies, carrying their heavy tools, and scattered home, while each one thought in their heart: "Today, I earned fifteen copper coins!"

Life

Private Tutor 245

— Zhengping

The position of a private tutor can hardly be considered a favorable one. This is not only because the salary is meager and insignificant, but also because the profession itself is unstable and insecure. A private tutor is mostly hired temporarily or for a short period. Even while in employment, they cannot avoid constantly feeling the threat of renewed unemployment. We know that most middle- and upper-class families hire private tutors to tutor their children in various major subjects in order to facilitate entrance exams or increase essential knowledge and have their needs. In such cases, the period specified on a private tutor's employment contract is probably only about three months. Some students who fail to enter school during the winter and summer vacations for various reasons, in order to facilitate their future schooling, also specifically hire a private tutor to tutor them in various important subjects. In such cases, the period of service is usually no more than ten months, or only four or five months at least. Naturally, there are also parents who particularly trust private tutors and employ them for longer periods, but such things are extremely rare.

Although the life of a private tutor is even more difficult than that of an ordinary school teacher, the number of people who long to obtain such a position is still countless. Of course, there are many people who are satisfied with obtaining such a position after receiving a diploma from a normal school or high school without obtaining corresponding knowledge. Even university graduates with "specialized knowledge" (?), In today's world where only one out of ten people can find a job, they also have to reach out to this insignificant position. Unemployed primary and secondary school teachers, as well as those who are engaged in the occupation of private tutors and are now idle, must also pay attention to this valuable position. The widespread unemployment of intellectuals has led to a widespread surplus of people who regard being a private tutor as a great hope.

Speaking of the remuneration of private tutors, I have a need to further mention their possible monthly income. This naturally has different numbers: the income can differ by tens or even hundreds of yuan, ranging from "salary not counted" to the more considerable income of those who have special introductions. Apart from warlords, bureaucratic politicians, big merchants, and compradors who are willing to pay heavy sums of more than one hundred yuan to hire full-time private tutors for their young masters and young ladies, the remuneration for a private tutor with teaching experience and good qualifications in ordinary middle- and upper-class families generally does not exceed fifty yuan a month. Last winter, a university graduate friend was hired by a doctor at a hospital affiliated with a certain coal mining company in Henan to tutor his own two children and the two children of his colleagues in Chinese, English, and mathematics, and he was still paid a monthly salary of fifty yuan. He also sent the invited teacher a travel allowance of twenty yuan. Another friend who graduated from the Department of Education of the University lost his teaching position in a certain middle school in another city. When he returned to Shanghai, thanks to the introduction of a friend, he immediately went to a certain mansion to impart his knowledge at the price of serving three hours a day and a monthly salary of forty yuan. The above is about male private tutors. As for female private tutors, it is even more affordable to sell their knowledge. There are also those who come out of universities and only hope to obtain this position for a small amount of thirty yuan, twenty-five yuan, twenty yuan, or even fifteen yuan a month, but they cannot get it. I have a female classmate who, after completing her third year of university, could not continue due to the lack of family economic ability and was forced to leave school to seek a living on her own. Because she was clever and capable, she simultaneously found two private tutor positions; she divided the two hours in the morning between one mansion and the two hours in the afternoon between another mansion. She was busy running around all day, spending three or four cents on trams and rickshaws every day, and her total income from the two places was only fifty yuan. I also know a lady who also came out of university. She once signed a three-month private tutor contract with a certain mansion in this city at a price of thirty yuan a month for three hours a day. There was also a friend's wife who declared that she was willing to sell the knowledge and labor that a private tutor could have for a monthly salary of fifteen yuan, but she did not get a buyer. We have the opportunity to see this kind of tragic fact fermented from this rotten society at any time.

Because private tutors must go to people's "homes" to teach, in order to save time and travel expenses, they (or she) need to move to live near the employer's mansion. This seems destined for them to constantly feel the burden of moving. Also, with a few exceptions, most employers rarely provide private tutors with both meals and accommodation; there are also those who only provide one meal. In this case, most of them must operate on their own. Because of the short-term and temporary nature of the occupation, their lives are naturally difficult to stabilize, so their greatest hope is to find a more stable occupation. A middle school teacher's position is probably their ideal goal, a primary school class teacher or subject teacher's position should also be very suitable for their appetite, and even an ordinary primary school teacher is considered a good position in their eyes. Most of their hopes are not easy to realize, so they are still unemployed most of the time.

In addition, there is another type of private tutor. They originally have a job. They may be a teacher in a primary or secondary school or a teacher in a night school or cram school. Because their income is not enough to maintain their lives, they must use their so-called "spare time" to grab a "side hustle" at people's mansions. It goes without saying how hard and busy these people are. I have a friend who teaches English in a certain middle school. In addition to teaching twelve hours a week, he also teaches six hours a week in a mansion. Every night, he also borrows a primary school to open a "special class" for employees and apprentices of some factories and shops to make up for English. Although his income is considerable, his hard work is not difficult for anyone to imagine.

Finally, I would like to mention the difficulties that private tutors can encounter. We know that private tutors are hired to teach several major subjects such as Chinese, English, and mathematics. Most people may not be proficient in all of these subjects. If a flaw is revealed in the explanation of a certain subject, or if a satisfactory answer cannot be given immediately to a question raised, the student's disbelief caused by this will cause great problems in the subsequent teaching process. It goes without saying that the student will not listen, and the employer's distrust will also be inevitable. At this time, it is naturally difficult for the teacher to maintain it.

Also, there are often great differences in the age and academic level of children in a family: the "class teaching" system is not applicable here, and you have to carefully guide them one by one. Although the number of students may not be very large, the troubles caused by the uneven level will certainly not be few. At this time, you can only teach patiently, and you must hold back the fire in your heart, so as not to cause unhappiness in your occupation due to your impatience. The "mansion" is not a place where you can afford to be angry, and those young masters and young ladies will not willingly look at your face. At this time, it is best to settle the account with "society", I think.

Art World

What Movies We Need to See 246

— Bing Jia

Recently, there has been a so-called soft versus hard argument in the film industry. Proponents of the soft approach believe that the sole purpose of movies is to provide the audience with sensual entertainment. Therefore, films should be romantic, sensual, and comedic. Proponents of the hard approach believe that the ultimate purpose of movies is not only to entertain the audience but also to educate them, providing the audience with spiritual and intellectual nourishment. Therefore, films should be, and must be, realistic and content-rich. I am not a film theorist, and I do not want to criticize these two opinions. I only want to provide them with some reference material from the standpoint of an audience member. However, before getting to the main topic, I must mention the reason for this debate and its importance.

×　×　×　×

Because movies are the closest to the average common people, the effectiveness of movies is greater than that of all art forms. They not only give the audience a concept but also provide action and imagery. Therefore, as soon as they emerge, they become powerful supporters of special social classes. That is, special social classes use them as tools to control the thinking of the average common people. In China, although film art is more immature than in Europe and the United States, its development and function are no exception. Just look, hasn't it developed from "The Burning of the Red Lotus Temple" to "Laughable Marriages," and then to "Sister Flowers" and "Mr. Wang"?

However, society is not a simple and static thing, and the masses (the common people) are not a unified whole. No matter how you inject anesthetics, you cannot stop the progress of society, and you cannot catch everyone in one net, making the masses forever unconscious. Some people will escape from your anesthesia. This forms an irreconcilable contradiction in the development of film art (as with any art): one is the supporter of special classes, and the other is the sustenance required by the masses themselves. This is the fundamental reason for the soft and hard film debate.

Currently, the number of people who refuse to be unconscious is increasing day by day. Therefore, on the one hand, mass art has become the only art movement, occupying the entire art scene. On the other hand, supporters of the old era are bound to fight back with all their might, forming the development of the entire restoration movement. Last year, the film art movement surged for a time, revealing a new opportunity for the future of film and producing many mass films, although most of them did not have the opportunity to be released. This is bound to make those old-fashioned figures in the film industry feel uneasy. They will inevitably, under the wings of the entire restoration movement, and like the "Classical Chinese Revival" in the literary world, extend their paper-thin fists to launch a counterattack. The "soft" versus "hard" debate shows that the film movement is no longer a time for closed-door innovation, nor is it just a time for theoretical struggle, but a time for head-on clashes for survival.

×　×　×　×

So, what about us, standing in the position of the audience? What kind of movies do we need? Simply put, we need hard films and not soft films. We are in a difficult era, and our lives are extremely difficult. Of course, we desperately need entertainment and sensual comfort, but not as the proponents of the soft approach imagine, that as long as there are passionate hugs, kisses, and women's legs, we will be happy to the point of unconsciousness. No! Absolutely not! We need intellectual stimulation far more than we need physical stimulation. We want to laugh, but we don't laugh meaninglessly. We want to gain a little life function from movies before we laugh. All our educational opportunities and cultural nourishment have been completely deprived. Movies are a simple and clear way to increase our knowledge and life force. If we only treat them as entertainment, wouldn't we be cutting ourselves off from culture and starving ourselves to death? For example, the simultaneous release of "Song of the Fishermen" and "Mr. Wang" actually gave the proponents of the soft approach a merciless blow. The frivolous tunes of "Mr. Wang" ultimately could not defeat the ability of "Song of the Fishermen" to obtain a wide audience due to its life content. This is not forced, but our audience's actual demand.

I hope that movie audiences will judge the outcome of the soft and hard debate based on our actual demands!

International Radio Station

New Children's Cultural Construction in the Soviet Union 247

— Translated by Yangzi from the Japanese work of Shigezaku Niijima

Where do these spirited, rosy-cheeked Soviet schoolchildren go after school? Do they go home? Do they go to their mothers? I don't think so. Because most Soviet children's parents are working in factories or institutions during the day (because there is no unemployment in the Soviet Union), and they go to training courses at night.

(1) For the Systematic Facilities of Children's Education

First, schools are devising methods for children's time outside of school. Second, adult cultural facilities are provided to children at certain times. All theaters hold special morning performances so that older children can appreciate magnificent dramas. Movie theaters also screen selected films specifically for children. Various workers' clubs are conducting activities among children. Cultural parks have special "children's villages," and general sports fields or swimming pools are open to these playful children at certain times. In addition, there is a network of various children's facilities, artistic children's education centers, children's theaters, children's movie theaters, technical labor practice centers or libraries, consultation offices for small trips or large trips, children's education clubs, etc.

(2) Children's Theater

Although the first children's theater
